    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer17215729455742980779">A straight from the shoulder look at life in which I ask some awkward questions; such as, ‘Who am I?’, ‘Where did I come from?’, ‘What am I doing here?’ and ‘Why do <i>we</i> resist change?’ If at this point you’re tempted to flick through this book looking for the answers, save yourself the trouble - you won’t find any. This isn’t a book of answers - it’s a book of self-reflecti</span>
  <span id="freeText17215729455742980779" style="display:none">A straight from the shoulder look at life in which I ask some awkward questions; such as, ‘Who am I?’, ‘Where did I come from?’, ‘What am I doing here?’ and ‘Why do <i>we</i> resist change?’ If at this point you’re tempted to flick through this book looking for the answers, save yourself the trouble - you won’t find any. This isn’t a book of answers - it’s a book of self-reflective questions that have fascinated me all of my life. Reflecting on them has given new meaning and purpose to my life and changed not only the way I see the world, but the way I see you too. When we change our mind … we <i>also</i> change our world.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6984663819975410166">I gave this book five stars due to the fact that, with it's help, I have finally been enlightened to change my life for the better and, I am in the process of doing so. Definitely not a book to read quickly. This book requires a great amount of thought from the reader. Took me awhile to finish and actually digest it.   <span id="freeText6984663819975410166" style="display:none">I gave this book five stars due to the fact that, with it's help, I have finally been enlightened to change my life for the better and, I am in the process of doing so. Definitely not a book to read quickly. This book requires a great amount of thought from the reader. Took me awhile to finish and actually digest it. I am ecstatic that I took the necessary time to do so.<br />Coming into this world with no physical possessions and passing out of this world with no physical possessions has to make one think that our true purpose, in this life, should be more from a higher level of consciousness than what the majority of mankind are capable of expressing, through their actions, in their lifetimes.<br />I highly recommend taking the time to read On the Other Hand. I thank Renee Paule for the opportunity to read this book and I look forward to reading her other books.</span>

<div id="review_1979049948" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1979049948" />
    <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea"><img alt="Amalia Gkavea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559158764p2/56789747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1979049948?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amalia Gkavea" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea">Amalia Gkavea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9782954681139" href="/book/show/21782513-on-the-other-hand">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=psychology-mentality">psychology-mentality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=sociology">sociology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1979049948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14336525762430244253"><i>
  <b>''There's an air of decency implied in the expression 'human being'; it doesn't quite fit with the way we behave.''</b>
</i><br/><br/>Do not let the cute, charming front cover fool you. This isn’t a ‘self-help’ book in the mundane sense of the genre, it is rather a ‘self- awareness’ book that poses questions that, most probably, we’ve all thought at certain points of our lives, but have been too afraid to ask. I know I have and I am only 32.<br/><br/>‘’On the Other Hand’’...such a fitting title. Renee brings so many que</span>
  <span id="freeText14336525762430244253" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>''There's an air of decency implied in the expression 'human being'; it doesn't quite fit with the way we behave.''</b>
</i><br /><br />Do not let the cute, charming front cover fool you. This isn’t a ‘self-help’ book in the mundane sense of the genre, it is rather a ‘self- awareness’ book that poses questions that, most probably, we’ve all thought at certain points of our lives, but have been too afraid to ask. I know I have and I am only 32.<br /><br />‘’On the Other Hand’’...such a fitting title. Renee brings so many questions into focus, presenting the various sides of each argument but doesn’t provide direct answers. This is what makes a big difference from other examples of the genre,and this is the main reason I’ve enjoyed this book so much.She allows us to stop and contemplate, and presents her own side in a subtle, warm way without imposing anything on the reader., In my opinion, this makes the message of the book even more powerful and the impact, at least on me, was significant. She touches upon subjects that we all face daily. Insecurity, memories, acceptance, independence, belief, life and death, and the list goes on...As I’m writing this review, my mind wonders in today's bleak news. My uncle passed away having lost a short battle with cancer,and her passage about death suddenly acquired a deeper, more personal meaning.Another subject that stood out, for me, was fear. For the first time, I came across a definition for this dreadful feeling that has been my plague for many years, and reading this helped me understand it a bit better.<br /><br />As other reviewers have mentioned, this book isn’t a light read and it’s not for the faint of heart. It is raw and honest, too honest at certain points. You may come across passages that will challenge convictions you have retained for years, you may even disagree with some of the arguments presented. It doesn’t matter, do not let that dissuade you. Everyone has a different opinion and this is the basis of every healthy arguments. At least, it should be...So, perhaps next time, we may allow ourselves ask these big questions and end up being less dogmatic and more accepting…<br /><br />Many, many sincere thanks to Renee for providing me with the opportunity to read ‘’On the Other Hand’’.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14336525762430244253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2067647136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15063165992163970726">Renée Paule has the rare gift of letting you see yourself more clearly by reflecting on the big questions. She is never preachy or righteous as she lays before you a banquet of her life experiences; letting you sample what you like, but never forcing you to put anything on your plate that you do not want. Many readers will appreciate the Socratic methodology that Renée uses to help you look at (your) life - telescope or microscope - your choice as to which lens you wish to focus on. Excellent su</span>
  <span id="freeText15063165992163970726" style="display:none">Renée Paule has the rare gift of letting you see yourself more clearly by reflecting on the big questions. She is never preachy or righteous as she lays before you a banquet of her life experiences; letting you sample what you like, but never forcing you to put anything on your plate that you do not want. Many readers will appreciate the Socratic methodology that Renée uses to help you look at (your) life - telescope or microscope - your choice as to which lens you wish to focus on. Excellent summer read that will help you put your life in perspective just in time for the new year.</span>

<div id="review_1511475550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1511475550" />
    <a title="Sanjay Gautam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10179929-sanjay-gautam"><img alt="Sanjay Gautam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427923732p2/10179929.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1985618221" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5117693611991688600"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>We can’t change the reflection without changing what is reflecting it.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><i> On the Other Hand</i> is written in a very deep manner. It provokes the thoughts. Makes us to see the world from a different point of view. It makes us to question everything we know. Why they exist? What are their purposes? You can say the whole message of this book is: "Think outside the box." <br/> <br/>This book raises many questions which we are probably aware of but hesitate to answer.   <span id="freeText5117693611991688600" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>We can’t change the reflection without changing what is reflecting it.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><i> On the Other Hand</i> is written in a very deep manner. It provokes the thoughts. Makes us to see the world from a different point of view. It makes us to question everything we know. Why they exist? What are their purposes? You can say the whole message of this book is: "Think outside the box." <br /> <br />This book raises many questions which we are probably aware of but hesitate to answer. Because we don't wanna know the answers. We criticise the things which we still use. We want them removed but they still exist because we don't <i> really</i> want them removed. Like we criticise media that mostly it shows negative news and sometimes we want it removed. But still it exists and we watch it almost daily. So why they will remove it if we still watch it?<br />This book is full of this type of examples. <br /><br />I really appreciate what this book was trying to convey. And I think the same that we must be curious. We must question things. But I also think there are some areas in which we can't <i>really</i> question things. We have to accept what we are told on the basis of written facts. Like I don't know exactly that the earth is a planet or not. It's ovel-shaped or not. Then how I will get to know these things? Of course from books and school. I can't go to space to see if it's really true or not, can I? It is just a general example. There are many more. <br /><br />Regardless, this book is great. Excellently written in a thought-provoking way. I can recommend it.<br /><br /><br /><b> <u> MY FAVOURITE LINES FROM THE BOOK </u></b><blockquote>
  <i>Technology has surpassed us and we carry it around as though it were an additional organ.<br /><br />Books can guide us but we must ask our own questions.<br /><br />We’re so involved, with television serials, the internet, the media, gossip, celebrities and the latest technology that we’ve no time left to recognise the magical world we live in.<br /><br />We’re given a blank sheet of paperto create our world on and we’ve scribbled all over it in the most horrible way; now we can’t read our own writing.<br /><br />We ignore the miracles that surround us; and then hope that one will drop into our laps.<br /><br />The parts of our nature we’re most uncomfortable with<br />is what we see and criticise in others.<br /><br />This is what we’ve become; competitive and ambitious for money; we stifle talent, curiosity and creativity because they’re not profitable pastimes. We’re encouraged to develop abilities that will prove to be commercial successes; this is a sad - and robotic - state of affairs.<br /><br />Human beings are diligent when it comes to searching for something they don’t really want to know or see; we know where not to look.<br /></i>
</blockquote>April 29, 2017</span>
  <a data-text-id="5117693611991688600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/23304855-on-the-other-hand">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54254365-yesha--books-teacup-and-reviews?shelf=non-fic">non-fic</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2051256072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5730622563583147237">(Note: I received review copy of this book from author, in exchange for an honest review. I am glad I got a chance to read this book.)<br/><br/>Throughout the books few things author has said repeatedly and very clearly- First, you need to question everything. Questions are more important than answers. If you keep questioning, you understand the depth and value of questions. I found this very reasonable thing to do. I loved one example author gave in the book which I found very agreeable, the teaching sys</span>
  <span id="freeText5730622563583147237" style="display:none">(Note: I received review copy of this book from author, in exchange for an honest review. I am glad I got a chance to read this book.)<br /><br />Throughout the books few things author has said repeatedly and very clearly- First, you need to question everything. Questions are more important than answers. If you keep questioning, you understand the depth and value of questions. I found this very reasonable thing to do. I loved one example author gave in the book which I found very agreeable, the teaching system. We never question anything we are taught by teachers or parents who were taught by their teachers and so on. We just accept it without questioning. And if we do we are labelled “odd”. This reminded me of the movie, ‘Mr. Peabody &amp; Sherman’ in which father and son time travels to learn actual history which turned out quite different than we are taught in school.<br /><br />Second, you need to change if you want to change everything around you. Start with yourself. This was not something new that author has said, we are listening this quite often but no one stick to it. I liked author’s style of making us realize why we need to do it. The question and thought provoking topic she covered this point throughout the book like, interaction, open-mindedness, cluttered mind, Comfort &amp; security, fear, and many more.<br /><br />Another thing was TV/Radio/Social Medias confuses everything more. Now I’m neutral for this. You can’t blame everything on government as the government is formed by humans only. This I liked and I do agree with author here. Author encourages to view the world from another perspective, don’t be hypocrite and stereotype, and question everything.<br /><br />And as for the answers, that you have to find yourself. The books will lead you though the different points and questions of that point to make it easier to find and understand questions. Book is not claiming to have all answers and also as author said it’s impossible to have all answers in this life time but this can change your view point towards the world and more toward yourself.<br /><br />I felt this book need open, clear and adapting mind to understand very plain unveiled truth. As it is said in the blurb “it brings you face to face with yourself … but not the one you see when you look in the mirror.” So whoever is ready to face the questions, this book is for them. This is definitely heavy read, not a quick read and it does have thought changing effect. This is a kind of book I will reopen again and will read again. The more you re-read the more you understand.<br /><br />I would say take your own time to read this book. It’s not one sitting book. On the Other Hand brought me back from fantasy, YA world to the reality.<br /><br /> <a href="https://booksteacupnreviews.wordpress.com/2017/07/09/on-the-other-hand-the-little-anthology-of-big-questions-by-renee-paule/" rel="nofollow noopener">Read full Review on my blog here</a><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10999390599351250329">This is a book you should definitely buy, if you are interested in finding more about yourself as a person and about the world around you, if you are interested in raising questions, given the fact that sometimes you will not find answers or you will find many answers for the same question.It is a heart to heart talk between author and reader.I found out so much about myself from this book, i found so many of my thoughts here, thoughts i was not completely aware of.I love the author,s style of w</span>
  <span id="freeText10999390599351250329" style="display:none">This is a book you should definitely buy, if you are interested in finding more about yourself as a person and about the world around you, if you are interested in raising questions, given the fact that sometimes you will not find answers or you will find many answers for the same question.It is a heart to heart talk between author and reader.I found out so much about myself from this book, i found so many of my thoughts here, thoughts i was not completely aware of.I love the author,s style of writing, the way she talks to the reader, sharing her personal life experience, her ideas, her soul.This book is about life, about questions, about who we are, about our actions.Despite the fact that this book has only 136 pages, it covers many topics completely:the world, society, rules, open-mindedness, interaction, what is truly important and what is not, different views on things, time, right, wrong, light, shadow, visible, invisible, awareness, where we truly are, curiosity and confusion, our mind, change, information, evolution of technology and how it affects us all, comfort, security, absurdities, fears, actions, freedom, definition of ourselves.This book is a completely different view on things, it is about re-thinking on everything that we are, that society is.I enjoyed this book so much, i say it again, it is so easy to read but read it carefully, so you can truly understand what the author has to say.I read it quickly but i forgot to change my status here in goodreads, after i finished it reading.I give it 5 stars, because i found myself in this book, it gave light to my eyes, i received answers, also i realized there are so many more questions to be raised.Life is a rollercoaster.This review is entirely objective, but thank you Renee Paule again for allowing me to have this book, now i understand everything.</span>

<div id="review_760859391" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/760859391" />
    <a title="G.R. Hewitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25247349-g-r-hewitt"><img alt="G.R. Hewitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505231848p2/25247349.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/760859391?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="G.R. Hewitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="G.R. Hewitt" href="/user/show/25247349-g-r-hewitt">G.R. Hewitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25247349-g-r-hewitt?shelf=motivational">motivational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25247349-g-r-hewitt?shelf=inspirational">inspirational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25247349-g-r-hewitt?shelf=self-help">self-help</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25247349-g-r-hewitt?shelf=self-awareness">self-awareness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25247349-g-r-hewitt?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25247349-g-r-hewitt?shelf=spiritual">spiritual</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25247349-g-r-hewitt?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25247349-g-r-hewitt?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25247349-g-r-hewitt?shelf=thought-provoking">thought-provoking</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer760859391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1575628783528449372">First of all, I must declare an interest in this book as I know the author very well and I edited the book for her. I have not and will not be paid for my services in any way. This book stands on its own merit and needs no props or bias. It is from this standpoint that I am pleased to write my review.<br/><br/>*****<br/><br/>If you are looking for answers to the questions in this book you will be disappointed; there are no `answer pages' at the back. Rather, the author invites you to think about life by taking anot</span>
  <span id="freeText1575628783528449372" style="display:none">First of all, I must declare an interest in this book as I know the author very well and I edited the book for her. I have not and will not be paid for my services in any way. This book stands on its own merit and needs no props or bias. It is from this standpoint that I am pleased to write my review.<br /><br />*****<br /><br />If you are looking for answers to the questions in this book you will be disappointed; there are no `answer pages' at the back. Rather, the author invites you to think about life by taking another look at it. This is not an easy-street-read pandering to the masses. The overriding theme of this book is that we are responsible for ourselves and the things that happen to us; not a popular concept in this `there, there' placating world where we point the finger everywhere but at ourselves.<br /><br />This book points no fingers but looks at the human race, as a whole. With that thought in mind the book asks:<br /><br />"Why do we do these things?" The book "... explores these facets with some bold and frank questions that can make for uncomfortable reading."<br /><br />and states:<br /><br />"Be prepared ... old beliefs are hard to eliminate and to let go of. I write nothing you have to believe. I ask you to believe nothing. I do try to show you that Humanity created this world and only Humanity can dismantle it".<br /><br />If you are prepared or want to make changes to your life then I recommend this work. By the time you are done reading it you may have a whole new perspective on the world we all have to live in. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1575628783528449372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1099851969147282256">: On The Other Hand: The Little Anthology of Big Questions (Paperback)<br/>I have struggled to write this review.<br/>First, I found the book difficult to digest... I chewed over it, slowly.<br/>The author rather sternly points to the importance of 'being prepared to be brutally honest'...<br/>My core-beliefs are not in alignment with some of her assertions and I struggled at times with the seemingly, to me, relentless questions. (As a beloved friend of mine will atest, erotemes are not my favourite punctuation!)<br/><br/>So</span>
  <span id="freeText1099851969147282256" style="display:none">: On The Other Hand: The Little Anthology of Big Questions (Paperback)<br />I have struggled to write this review.<br />First, I found the book difficult to digest... I chewed over it, slowly.<br />The author rather sternly points to the importance of 'being prepared to be brutally honest'...<br />My core-beliefs are not in alignment with some of her assertions and I struggled at times with the seemingly, to me, relentless questions. (As a beloved friend of mine will atest, erotemes are not my favourite punctuation!)<br /><br />So, I would say if you enjoy analytical and 'why' exploration, you are in for a treat, however you may need to push yourself to wade in deeper if you prefer a gentler and sweeter approach to your 'wake-up calls' :)<br /><br />The actual body of work Renee has created makes sense, and much is in complete alignment with my own realisations. With personal courage she challenges so many of Society's sacred cows, and I would happily stand shoulder to shoulder with her in this.<br /><br />'Culture' is part of the inheritance we are 'passing on' to the next generation. Before that, Renee would like us to question what exactly is IN that parcel; What if it's just a junk box full of 'Rules and Regulations'?<br /><br />I love the original art work of the quirky young Miss seated on her books, cosy in a sweater decorated with a reflected question mark.<br />Another delight is the "Who am I" poem ; ".....go IN, and find, the greatest prize"<br />Wise words indeed! A beautifully shared insight on practically everything you could think of, why not try it, and see if you agree too?</span>

          </span>

Every chapter explores significant life topics about things we prefer not to think about. I keep slipping back and I’m going to read it again. Love it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17693570507672331747">This book encourages you to look deep into yourself for answers to some thought provoking questions raised by the author.<br/><br/>Advocating neither science nor religion this book makes you stop and actually think about things, in a way that may never have occurred to you before.   <span id="freeText17693570507672331747" style="display:none">This book encourages you to look deep into yourself for answers to some thought provoking questions raised by the author.<br /><br />Advocating neither science nor religion this book makes you stop and actually think about things, in a way that may never have occurred to you before. It doesn't preach or condemn but asks you to think independently , prodding you to come up with answers to previously never thought of questions.<br /><br />A compulsive and stimulating read that grabs your attention and simply refuses to let go! A must read.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35991953-mariana-farcas?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1145638678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3250497066166268036">On the Other Hand: The Little Anthology of Big Questions <br/>This book is like a slow incubator, fiercely honest. Why we do what we do and why do we feel comfortable doing it? Rules, traditions?<br/>On the Other Hand raises more questions than it answers. Recommended to teenagers and young adult.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4410394560664209293">'On the other hand' is a book unlike most I have read for a long time. In the Socratic tradition of asking questions, this book is sort of a series of questions to ask yourself to understand your true self. <br/>At the face of it, the book may seem like a difficult read as the relentless and unending series of questions and no obvious answers seems to be coming from the author herself. The questions also zoom in and zoom out in a bit of unstructured way.<br/>But what is most remarkable for me about this b</span>
  <span id="freeText4410394560664209293" style="display:none">'On the other hand' is a book unlike most I have read for a long time. In the Socratic tradition of asking questions, this book is sort of a series of questions to ask yourself to understand your true self. <br />At the face of it, the book may seem like a difficult read as the relentless and unending series of questions and no obvious answers seems to be coming from the author herself. The questions also zoom in and zoom out in a bit of unstructured way.<br />But what is most remarkable for me about this book is actually Renee's own background and how she has managed to stay so positive, curious, and open-minded despite that. In essence, that's the true testament to the power of this book.<br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TlQrptcPlQmvMcGOhDRfS5h6sBOIG/u1e8yfVcVpWp26TJJB9gJEOFTCd2r/yHKXfNlEpUmKeHOEfPdjvUsKwA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hx4xeFhrIs9GCN68xSGLtw9I+qbs8CD0YwB4pDRSt7RzBoifeWbz/r37aFi+3aZr6+sOEC1hozKcsBCSTHDn6Q==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7376084.Ren_e_Paule">About Renée Paule</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7376084.Ren_e_Paule"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1551894100p3/7376084.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7376084.Ren_e_Paule">Renée Paule

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4357624040045898307"><b>'Self-reflection', 'Know Thyself' and 'Semi-autobiography'</b><br/><br/>'Top of the morning' from Ireland.<br/><br/>Many years ago I wrote my autobiography - probably more as therapy than anything else - but life continued happening to me and I got to thinking, what good will this story do, isn’t there enough misery in the world without me adding to it? I subsequently burnt the manuscript. It was around that time that I </span>
  <span id="freeText4357624040045898307" style="display:none"><b>'Self-reflection', 'Know Thyself' and 'Semi-autobiography'</b><br /><br />'Top of the morning' from Ireland.<br /><br />Many years ago I wrote my autobiography - probably more as therapy than anything else - but life continued happening to me and I got to thinking, what good will this story do, isn’t there enough misery in the world without me adding to it? I subsequently burnt the manuscript. It was around that time that I began searching for meaning in my life and had a profound experience - a realisation that we’re all connected; we’re One. In my books, I take an honest look at our quirky and often bizarre behaviour in society and challenge the status-quo we accept as unchangeable - questioning and pushing the boundaries we set ourselves, and those that have been set for us. I’m convinced that if we want to change our lives and change our world then we must first change ourselves. I invite you to join me on my journey, questioning the society we call ours and the role we play within it.<br /><br /><u>My Reviews</u><br />I rate/review books that have given me pause for thought. 5 stars = something resonated with me.<br /><br />Author Interviews, Articles and Questionnaires are at:<br /><br /><a href="https://pebbleinthestillwaters.blogspot.ie/2014/07/author-interview-renee-paule-on-other.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Pebble in the Still Waters</a><br /><a href="https://www.smashwords.com/profile/view/reneepaule" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Smashwords</a><br /><a href="https://twogalsandabook.com/2017/04/17/just-around-the-bend-by-renee-paule-interview-giveaway/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Two Girls and a Blog</a><br /><a href="https://readrantrockandroll.com/2017/04/17/just-around-the-bend-by-renee-paule/#more-3129" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Read, Rant and Rock and Roll</a> - <i>Just Around the Bend</i><br /><a href="https://booksteacupnreviews.wordpress.com/2017/07/09/on-the-other-hand-the-little-anthology-of-big-questions-by-renee-paule/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Books, Teacup and Reviews</a><br /><a href="https://www.bookworks.com/2017/09/first-book-learning-curve-experience/#comment-8387" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">BookWorks</a><br /><a href="https://readrantrockandroll.com/2017/10/02/the-frightened-little-flower-bud-by-renee-paule-and-godfrey-r-hewitt-book-review-and-author-interviews/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Read, Rant and Rock and Roll</a> <i>- The Frightened Little Flower Bud</i><br /><br />Show good will to each other - every day.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4357624040045898307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
